Diary of the British Wimbledon World Tennis Championships (3) Special Correspondence from London - Aspiration 193

June 30th (Friday)

Today, although there were no major events, an unexpected change occurred, just like Faqua's defeat of Panlai on Wednesday. Nees defeated Cedar in three straight sets, and Lee had won the first two sets against Stokes, and was leading 3-1. This game undoubtedly gave the resident players a great shock, but in fact, there is enough to comfort and explain themselves, because Stokes has exhausted his strength, with greatly improved skills, to defeat a Lee who was extremely exhausted. The weather was very warm, full of humidity, and the sun alternated with white clouds, but it did not seem to have two intentions. The audience was still large. Those who could not enter the Central Court or the First Court surrounded other outer courts, quietly listening to the applause from the Central and First Courts. The closing match of the First Court was Mrs. Maddy against Mrs. Henroding. The French woman won a total of only three games, all in the first set. Mrs. Maddy was slightly lax and made many unnecessary mistakes. Afterwards, she worked hard, without any leniency, and defeated Henroding with machine-like balls.

The match between Cedar and Hughes followed. Cedar won the first three games, and although he resisted strongly, he did not panic. Afterwards, Hughes won nine games in the next thirteen games. Cedar was unable to take advantage of opportunities. Although his hitting technique was not relaxed and optimistic, this mixed method could not be practical against a player who never lost his confidence and gradually increased his strength. Hughes had nothing to lose and was always in the lead, with excellent judgment, careful, courageous, and able to advance in time. Most of the time, Cedar attacked with a close and powerful forehand draw, and the ball hit the racket like an explosion.

In the first and second sets, there is no need to elaborate. Cedar's strategy was not bad, but his method was wrong. He could take the lead with confidence and understanding, but he could not maintain it. A game or a set often required a winning shot, but it was obtained by Hughes. The first and second sets were exactly the same, only the second set was lost more easily. Cedar's eyesight also deteriorated greatly. Often, he could see the falling ball, but Cedar wanted to hit it but missed it. There were too many mistakes compared to usual, often sending the ball into the net or slightly out of bounds.

Later, he was subjected to heavy pressure again, but he was bold and intelligent. Hughes may have given his best performance ever and continued to improve. Every shot was taken with risk. If it was successful, he would not regret it. He won the first set with nine to seven, followed by seven to five. Cedar's defeat was well deserved. The overall game was 15% to 50% worse than his usual performance.

The third set started wrong again, but he gradually recovered and took a 3-1 lead. Suddenly, he collapsed from there, unable to win a single game. His luck was also too bad, often with balls that seemed good, but the result was the opposite. Hughes had the feeling of controlling the enemy. In the last few games, his momentum was unstoppable. Cedar fell into despair. Hughes had better stamina on the court than Cedar. Cedar seemed to have suffered from heatstroke in the second set, leaning on a chair to rest, drinking a large amount of water, wiping himself with a towel, and covering his head and neck with a wet towel. Hughes showed no signs of fatigue and was ready to continue the game at any time.

Baihong Track and Field Team's Opinions on the National Games 196

The Baihong Track and Field Team submitted a document to the National Games Preparatory Committee on the ninth of this month, stating: "Submitting opinions for adoption and implementation. Since the Preparatory Committee announced that the games would be held on Double Ten Festival this year, the national sports community has shown a lively atmosphere. In the future, the gathering in the capital will be promising. Our team has been practicing track and field for many years. Regarding this conference, regarding the number of places and events under the track and field category, we would like to express our humble opinions. If they can be adopted, we would be very fortunate.

㈠ The number of places should be changed to a six-person system, and it should be stipulated that each unit's athletes attending each event should not exceed four people at most. In our country's National Games track and field category, the number of places for each event has always only been four. However, it is found that there are more than thirty participating provincial and municipal units in the National Games, and there should be no fewer than five or six hundred track and field athletes. With five or six hundred people competing for a small number of places, their efforts are equally matched. There will inevitably be many people who fail to make the list due to a slight difference. It is found that modern sports meets with a larger scale, not to mention them, the Japanese National Games also take six places. This embodies the purpose of selecting true talents and encouraging future generations. In the budding era of sports in our country, this system seems to be urgently emulated. Moreover, sports in our country are not only immature, but also unevenly developed. Shanghai, Ping, Ji, and Yue are roughly scaled, while the provinces in the interior are just starting. In the previous Hangzhou National Games, all the championships were won by the stronger units, and the inland units failed to win anything. Although this conforms to the formula of the superior winning and the inferior being eliminated, the inland sports will inevitably become more boring after this blow. If this system can be adopted, and it is stipulated that each province and city unit attending track and field events should be limited to a maximum of four athletes per event, then any strong provincial and municipal unit will never be able to monopolize all the places. There must be one or two positions left for the weaker units to compete for. This can arouse the interest of inland sports and achieve the effect of universal development.

㈡ Various events should strive to follow the current events of the World Games and expand sports in our country. We should not only aim at the Far East, but should broaden our horizons and aim at the world. It is found that the track and field events of the World Games have more events than the National Games, including the 3000-meter steeplechase, 5000 meters, marathon, race walking, and hammer throw. Our country should not abandon them just because the Far East Games do not have them. We should immediately adopt them and list them as National Games events. If there is a short time and various places have not been prepared, it may be temporarily designated as a performance, and various units should be notified to participate as much as possible.

Whether the above two points are appropriate, I hope to be given a discussion. I am very much looking forward to it. This is presented to the National Games Preparatory Committee.

Page 16

Spring and Autumn

Hunger 199

— Zuo Yun

'Hunger.' This word does not need to be explained literally. Those who are full all day long will never understand how miserable the state of hunger is.

In the Dongxinqiao and Great World areas, the 'wild chickens' stand erect on the streets. Why do they stand from afternoon until midnight every day, and sometimes use dragging and binding methods on pedestrians? Are they satisfying their sexual desires? This is entirely hunger urging them to use despicable and lowly methods to satisfy the panic of their stomachs.

Now it's better. The French Concession police authorities, in order to maintain order on the roads and the peace of pedestrians, have uniformly prohibited them from operating outside. Recently, many have been detained in the patrol room. This is almost taking away the rice bowl in their hands. It is a terrible thing to not allow a person to eat!

We must come back to the point. Of course, wild chickens soliciting customers outside has a very bad influence on both society and individuals. We are also very sympathetic to the crackdown. But hunger is the same for everyone. For example, sometimes when my meal is cooked late, my stomach will rumble and make a lot of noise, urging me to eat.

Imagine, what is the rumbling in the stomachs of those who have no hope of eating? It must be intensely unfair, and the result is that rebellious emotions are produced in this unstable situation. The strong take risks and do all kinds of evil deeds. The weak commit suicide, become beggars, or engage in the flesh trade. So becoming a 'wild chicken' is not their own will, and of course it is inseparable from the background of hunger.

Since the sins of society are created in an environment of hunger, then society should think of ways to eliminate the fact of hunger. But, on the contrary, society is constantly creating the background of hunger; bankers desperately concentrate money, capitalists desperately seek self-sufficiency, big merchants desperately monopolize business:::: there is no need to say more. There are many people in society who exploit others by virtue of their status and power, all of whom are seizing the food of the majority to cultivate themselves, so the formation of hunger is a very common phenomenon.

The fact of hunger has become widespread, and many people do not know the feeling of hunger. Those who are hungry and those who are not hungry are separated. Naturally, this word "hunger" will always occupy an important page in the dictionary.

O God of Hunger! May you forever occupy a separate position in people's stomachs!

Summer Clouds, Many Strange Peaks 200

— Lin Ying

Tired of reading at noon, put down the book and take a nap, this is exactly the life of summer. But you are in the depths of the willow shade, looking up at the sky, and the layers of white clouds transform into many patterns. Some are like cowherds riding cows, some are like warriors dancing swords, no matter how you imagine them, they are all excellent natural paintings. Therefore, I feel that the ancients' saying that "summer clouds have many strange peaks" is not wrong at all.

Most people think that the most difficult thing to grasp is a woman's psychology, but I think the most difficult thing to grasp is the weather in summer. When you go out, the scorching sun radiates heat, scorching your skin; but maybe in a flash, a gust of cool wind comes, and the white clouds immediately turn into dark clouds, and the rain drops as big as beans splash down, catching people off guard. If you bring an umbrella and galoshes, it just doesn't rain.

Most of the fashionable women nowadays wear thin gauze like cicada wings, and their snow-white skin is faintly visible. The tailoring of new clothes is in harmony with the curves of the body, almost like wrapping. Wearing wobbly high-heeled shoes, if you encounter a sudden rain, you want to avoid dancing and dancing, and as a result, you are soaked like Yang Guifei emerging from a bath, allowing the poor people to appreciate this graceful beauty; I really feel embarrassed for them.

However, what is more changeable than summer clouds and summer rain is the political views of the adults and gentlemen. Today it is going east, tomorrow it will go west, making it simply difficult for subordinates to serve. Unless they are roundworms in their stomachs, this is how they know their intentions, otherwise a move will guarantee that you will not be reprimanded, but you will also encounter a rubber nail.

Night-Wandering Gentleman 201

— Qing Qu

I say "Night-Wandering Gentleman," and someone asks who is that person's name? I reply to him that this term is not a person's nickname, but a small "firefly." Fireflies often shine in the dark at night, and they will flash in our eyes, which is very beautiful. Therefore, although the firefly is a very small kind of insect, the ancients gave it many names, which I really cannot list. The most interesting one can be considered the four characters "Night-Wandering Gentleman," which I feel is especially accurate and immovable, and worth talking about!

This kind of insect, in its early stage, also resembles mosquitoes, close to beetles, and its color is slightly yellow. If zoologists summarize it, they would have to call it a "sheathed wings" type. However, its hair ends are rich in phosphorus, so it naturally emits a kind of cold light, like the noctiluca on the sea. Isn't this a unique feature in the insect world? Not only that, the hotter the weather, the stronger its luminous power is in the middle of the night. Children often enjoy the cool in the courtyard, and it just happens to fly down from the corner of the wall and eaves. In a short while, it has been patted under the cattail fan and put into a gourd-shaped glass bottle. Childhood is inherently good, and when the night is quiet and late, and they are lying down to sleep, they put it by the pillow. You! If you want to read, you can read ten lines at a glance, very clearly, or hang it in the middle of the tent, which can be regarded as a naturally formed small electric lamp that can illuminate until dawn. Therefore, "fireflies" are a kind of grace for children. It is said that in North America, there are many natives who, when walking into the forest at night, fear that the darkness will cause them to lose their way, and they capture very large "fireflies" and tie them between the toes of their feet. Walking is still like walking under the moon! The Sui Emperor of our country once went out for a night tour one day, and the history books record that he released several bushels of fireflies. In an instant, the light was like daytime. Although it is unavoidable to say too much, I think that if someone gathers them together and deeply studies their life and breeding methods, not only is it a very fun skill, but it can be said that its effect is not small, and it is more appropriate to call it "Mingdeng" rather than calling it "Gongzi," which is truly worthy of the name.

New Inventions by Chinese Inventors 205

— Transmitted from Ji

Recently, China has produced quite a few inventors. For example, Mr. Tang Zhongming, who invented charcoal as a substitute for gasoline, caused quite a stir for a time, earning the praise of the Ministry of Industry. He even conducted a field test on the long-distance bus route between Nanjing and Tangshan, and it is said that the results were very satisfactory. Mr. Wang Richang from Hubei invented an anti-aircraft arrow, which was tested in the open space of the barracks near the Nanyang Tobacco Factory in Hankou. It reached a height of 4,000 meters and exploded in the air at 30 meters, with very good results. Mr. Huang Zhirong, a technician at the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department's Ordnance Repair Factory in Zhenjiang, invented a new type of portable machine gun that can freely operate the safety mechanism. Turning it left allows for rapid firing, while turning it right allows for single firing. A bayonet can also be mounted on top of the machine gun. Rapid firing is like a continuous stream of bullets, extraordinarily sharp. It is said that the authorities will forward it to the central government for commendation. Mr. Fan Zhenjiang from Bian invented a two-section mortar, with a long shooting range, reaching up to 7,000 meters, exceeding the range of anti-aircraft guns. His father, Guoliang, also invented an assault steel plate vehicle. In addition, a student, Mr. X, from Tongji University invented a private secret wireless radio, and a student from Hunan University invented a trackless train. It is said that the test results were all good. These inventors have all emerged within the past year or two. In China, where the level of science is backward, this can be considered quite encouraging. However, these inventions are like flashes in the pan, and are not seen in formal use anywhere. They appear like a dragon, showing only the head and not the tail. I cannot help but sigh in regret for the inventors!

Some people say that China's invention endeavors will never have good results, because the children of wealthy people indulge in pleasure and are absolutely unwilling to spend years diligently studying these troublesome things. People without money, although interested in science, have no money to buy reference books, no money to purchase experimental materials, and even less money to attend school. Even if there are one or two talented scientists, they cannot freely develop their talents due to environmental constraints. Therefore, those who want to study science cannot find a way in, and those who have already found a way stop their research work midway. This statement has some merit, but I think this is not the absolute reason!

The inventor of the microscope, Leeuwenhoek (Dutch), initially worked as a copyist for others. The inventor of the steamboat, Fulton (American), was so poor that he relied on his mother's work to make a living. The inventor of the railway, Stephenson (British), was originally a cowherd. The inventor of the light bulb, movies, and phonograph, Edison (American), went to work as a train attendant on the Canadian railway at the age of twelve, which shows his poverty. It can be seen that people with scientific minds are not limited in the development of their talents due to difficult family lives. Then, the reason why China's recent inventors cannot contribute their research results to society, nor can they promote and develop their research work, certainly has its own special reasons, and is definitely not entirely limited by poverty. These special reasons are nothing more than the following two:

(1) The government does not provide rewards and assistance. (2) Domestic disasters occur frequently, making it impossible to continue their research work with peace of mind.

The above two points are only part of the special reasons that hinder the invention endeavors, and are not insurmountable obstacles. After Morse (American) invented the telegraph, he first reported it to the government, but the government ignored him. After Galileo (Italian) invented the telescope, although he was hired by the King of Venice, he was angered by the Pope when he returned to his home country, who said that his book violated the Bible, and he was even taken to the church for severe torture. However, their inventions were eventually adopted by the world. If disasters occur frequently, it is impossible to study science with peace of mind, then how could there be an aviation king Karcher before and after the European war? It can be seen that anyone who is determined to study science cannot be suppressed by any obstacles. China's new inventors lack the courage to persevere. Although they have made small inventions, they become discouraged due to a temporary lack of material assistance or after suffering a blow, and eventually disappear without a trace. This is probably the main reason for their failure!

Book of Great Peace Under Heaven 206

— Qi Fan

Yesterday, Lin Yutang suddenly had a whim and expressed his opinion in this column: "Let the women do it," proposing to hand over all governing power to women, and he himself is determined to prepare to retire and go to Africa to learn to be a savage. This is indeed a very commendable opinion.

The "Book of Great Peace Under Heaven," a large book written by Liu Renhang, was first published in the early years of the Republic of China in 17 by the Shanghai Taidong Bookstore. The author named the book "Book of Great Peace Under Heaven" because he believed that the world could achieve peace immediately by following the book. His advocacy is self-proclaimed as the world's "Kun-transformationism," and its goal is to establish a world female government. What Liu Renhang says in his book is nothing more than that men value killing, while women are inclined to harmony and love. All the wars and killings in history have been caused by men, while women are the ones who give birth to people. He asks, "Do men become pregnant?" to show his unbreakable truth that men kill and women give life. Therefore, once women take charge of the government, they will definitely know that people are lovable and should be loved and not killed, war will be eliminated, and the world will be peaceful as a result.

In this way, it is indeed reasonable. If I add some supplements, then this reason will truly become undeniable, and the emergence of a female government should be promoted and will be endorsed by the masses, and the seeds of world harmony and peace will be obtained. The two sexes of men and women can indeed be called two major opposing classes, with women standing in the position of the oppressed. If we say that the modern problem lies in the opposition between the bourgeoisie and the proletariat, or the struggle of the fourth class against other classes, then what will follow will definitely be the opposition between men and women, the struggle of women against men. Modern workers get angry in the factory and go home to vent their anger on their wives and daughters. Rickshaw pullers who suffer losses from the police will also take revenge on their wives and daughters. Therefore, the oppression of women is even below the fourth class, so after the class struggle, there must be a struggle between the two sexes. The revolutionary struggle of the fourth class is still continuing to evolve, and the intensity of its harm is already enough to make people feel heartbroken. In the future, there is a possibility that it will be staged again and again, and the oppression of women has a longer history and a more severe degree of suffering, so once a women's revolution occurs, it must be the most cruel tragedy in the world. The current struggle almost has no formal female protagonist, so it is not the entire human race, but limited to the male gender, when the women's revolution occurs, it will be more extensive than the current, and the entire human race can not escape being swept into the whirlpool.

In order to avoid the occurrence of this tragedy, there is only one way for us men to surrender and lower our flags, like Lin Yutang's preparation to retire to Africa, which is one of the most brilliant methods. Liu Renhang's method is to first establish a world female government to prevent problems before they occur, which is even more clever. We Chinese people, in everything, love to fundamentally solve and thoroughly research, and pay attention to the way of long-term peace and stability, wholeheartedly hoping for peace under heaven and world harmony, and will definitely feel a twelve-point interest in what is said here. In school trials, there are also university students who elect female opera performers and actresses to be chairmen or presidents, which shows that if a female government is established, it will definitely be supported by a majority of people. Moreover, judging from the authority of school flowers and queens in schools today, it can be seen that the opinions of female governments are by no means frivolous. Hu Shih called on us to talk about the resistance against Japan in fifty years, and now we want to devote ourselves to cultivating national strength, so why not prepare for the world female government that should exist five thousand years from now? This is a matter of achieving peace under heaven and world harmony in one fell swoop, which is more worthy of effort than anything else, and besides, aren't we already moving in this direction?

Rationalization of English and Basic English 207

— Suo Yuan

There have already been two articles opposing Basic English in the North (see the "Beiping World Daily"), but they criticized Basic English from the perspective of an international language. As I understand it, Basic English is entirely an internal improvement problem of English, just like Japan's restriction of Chinese characters, and it is not what the advertisements say that it can be an international language. Here, I would like to criticize Basic English as a rationalization plan for English.

As I think, the rationalization of English should at least achieve the following two things:

The first is the rationalization of spelling, such as the vowel A, which has various different pronunciations, but the spelling all uses A. The same K and F sounds, but there are two spellings of C, K and F, PH. With KS and GZ, the extra X is added to make up the number. In addition, GHK, etc. in words such as Right know, etc. are not pronounced. These should be rationally transformed according to the principle of "one sound one letter, one letter one sound."

The second is the simplification of grammar. The irrational exceptions in English irregular verbs (Go-went-gone), exceptions to the plural of nouns (Foot-Feet-qoxes), and the addition of S to the third person singular present tense verbs: etc. should be rationally simplified, or even completely eliminated.

But what about Basic English? As evidenced by the various books that have been published, it completely inherits the irrational heritage of English in the above two points. Basic English mechanically stipulates a vocabulary of 850 words as its characteristic, but it is also its fatal flaw. Although the vocabulary of primitive humans is only more than 100 words, and the aborigines of Africa now only use more than 300 words, is that kind of primitive expression method of "a polished black circle with a dog drawn in front of a trumpet" applicable to modern people? That is a very obvious thing. The mechanical determination of the vocabulary makes Basic English become a "dead thing" and suffocates the possibility of the development of this language. If the originator does not regard Basic English only as a method of teaching English, and an inseparable appendage of English, but attempts to use Basic English as an independent language, a rationalization plan that can replace English, then it must be said that it is a complete failure.

This failure is by no means accidental. The work of rationalizing English will never be completed by Ogden, the director of the Language Research Institute of Cambridge University, who is a government-employed language scholar. For him, because of his position and the social class to which he belongs, he has neither the possibility of understanding language from a developmental perspective, nor the courage and strength to fundamentally transform English. At present, that kind of thorough rationalization will be severely criticized for "desecrating the sacredness of the national language" and "destroying the dignity of the grammar of the national language." The rulers of Great Britain only welcome Ogden's reformist deceptive schemes, because the true rationalization of English is beneficial to the British people, but unfavorable to the rulers.

However, the failure of Basic English is not enough to prove the impossibility of rationalizing English. English will still have a day when it is thoroughly rationalized by the British people themselves, just as the writing systems of China and Japan will complete true Romanization.

On Sequels 208

— Cao Juren

To ridicule sequels as evil works, as a snake's tail added to a sable coat; Jin Shengtan in the early Qing Dynasty was most impolite to "Romance of the West Chamber" and "Water Margin", referring to the part after "Grass Bridge" as a sequel by Guan Hanqing, and a generation of playwrights almost suffered injustice: as for "Water Margin", he simply cut off the part after the 70th chapter. After Yu Pingbo determined that the sequel to "Dream of the Red Chamber" was written by Gao E, the advantages and disadvantages of the upper and lower sections have been concluded, not only are "Completing the Dream" and "Repeating the Dream" superfluous. Yu Pingbo said: "There are no good sequels, not because the talent of the person writing the sequel must be far inferior to that of the predecessor, but because the talent and personality are different, just like their faces, if they are forced to follow each other, it will cause harm to both sides." ("Dream of the Red Chamber" first volume, page six) Mr. Qifan said: "Sequels are not easy to write, at least not as easy as creating a new path; there are also people who truly write sequels, but those who do well are still very few." These are all true insights and are very well said.

However, Jin Shengtan, Yu Pingbo, and Mr. Qifan all only argued from the perspective of literary creation; in the eyes of us who study history, "history" is almost devoid of creation, and every historical work is a sequel. The "Records of the Grand Historian" (史記), which has been praised for thousands of years, was preceded by "Genealogy of Emperors and Kings" (世本); after the Grand Historian, Sima Qian, Chu Shaosun, Liu Xiang, Liu Xin, Feng Shang, Yang Xiong, Feng Yan, Xiao Fen and a dozen or twenty others continued to revise the "Records of the Grand Historian." Ban Gu, the predecessor of the "Book of Han", was "Historical Records Post Transmission" written by his father Ban Biao. After Ban Gu, Ban Zhao and Feng Yan continued to write the book. Fan Ye's "Book of the Later Han" (後漢書) is as important as the "Book of Han" of Ban Gu; In fact, someone had already started writing during the Eastern Han Dynasty, Liu Zhen and Li You wrote "Annals and Tables of Famous Officials and Loyal Gentlemen Biographies of Imperial Relatives", and Cai Yong wrote "Two Records of Court Meetings and Chariot Clothing". In the early Jin Dynasty, Sima Biao wrote "Continuation of the Book of Han", and Hua Qiao revised "Records of Dongguan" into "Book of Later Han". Finally, Fan Ye compiled and deleted tedious additions and omissions, and wrote the "Book of the Later Han". When Fan Ye was arrested, the ten records were not yet completed, and Liu Zhao continued to complete them. Is the value of inheriting the achievements of predecessors, completing great works by continuing and supplementing, inferior to that of creation?

In the early Qing Dynasty, Huang Lizhou wrote "Cases of Confucian Scholars of the Ming Dynasty," wanting to use his full strength to organize the academic system of the Song and Yuan Dynasties over seven hundred years, setting down the outline to compile the "Cases of Scholars of Song and Yuan Dynasties." He was too old after all, and he died before the book was completed. He handed over all the work to his son Zong Yan to do, but Zong Yan did not compile it successfully either. All Zuwang devoted his life to continuing the "Cases of Scholars of Song and Yuan Dynasties", from the tenth to the nineteenth years of Qianlong, in these ten years, he supplemented and wrote "Cases of Scholars of Song and Yuan Dynasties" every year. After Zuwang died, the manuscript of the "Cases" was kept by his disciple Lu Hao, and Lizhou's great-grandson Zhigui borrowed it to transcribe, and then All Zuwang's son Pingfu corrected the errors and filled in the gaps, and wrote another version. It was not until the eighteenth year of Daoguang that the "Cases" were first printed, and Wang Xuanchen also corrected and supplemented them to complete one hundred volumes. A person's energy is limited, and a person's life is limited. A valuable work can never be completed by one person. In a world where all copyrights are owned, "sequels" are originally just profitable commodities, and it is almost regarded as a miracle to complete a work in half a century or a century by the strategy of the masses. But truly thinking for the sake of scholarship itself, and for the welfare of the community, even if it is a "sequel", isn't it an important part of great creation?

Therefore, I would like to add an explanation for Mr. Qifan. So-called undertakings always belong to the community; the Buddha said that all sentient beings and all inanimate things are created by the karma of all sentient beings. Literary creation, from the community becoming individual, and from the streets being confined to the study, is a unique deformity of modern times. Since ancient times, everyone participated in the work of creation in the chanting of ballads and the telling of stories, and it is almost impossible to know who is the creator and who is the continuer. The book "Water Margin" can only be said to be a joint creation of thousands of people over hundreds of years since the Southern Song Dynasty. Until today, storytellers in Eastern bookstores are still doing the work of writing sequels there. The time is coming soon when we will liberate from the study to the streets, and return from desk creation to community collective creation. I believe that the need for sequels in literature is no different from the need for sequels in historical works. "Copyright" is just a way to attract jade. Please Mr. Qifan talk about it again.

Tailor's Apprentice 209

— Cai Niansun

A-Xing slightly raised his head, secretly looking at the master who was smoking on the opposite side: The master tilted half of his head, facing the screen door, with the cigarette pipe blocked in his mouth, his thick lips laboriously buzzing, puffing and puffing. The paper was spinning on the cigarette pipe head, and the red flames reflected the master's face full of black beard, which was really interesting. But he dared not look too much, for fear of being noticed by the master, and quickly lowered his head, shrinking his eyes back to the sleeve he was holding in his hand.

Mechanically, stitch by stitch, sewing; the needle jumped up and down, and his head responded. Soon, one sleeve was finished, but another dropped.

The master turned his head and looked at him, and he was raising his head, oh no! He quickly lowered his head.

The master snorted in his nostrils, followed by two thick puffs of green smoke spewing out, directly towards him. He smelled a pungent smoky smell, and turned his face outward.

Another snort, heavier than before, and his heart pounded. He turned his outward face back, and kept his head lowered, his ears touching his shoulders.

The master was still puffing and puffing. The smoke was hitting him, and he endured the pungent smoky smell, his eyes fixed on his hands, not daring to move.

A-Xing was afraid of the master, especially the master's "hum". A-Xing was more than familiar with the master's "hum". For the past two years, the master had "hummed" almost every day; every time he "hummed", his heart would beat, and he would be afraid, afraid that the heavy tree root ruler would fall on his head. He realized that at that time, there would be patches on his head like desolate graves in the fields, swelling high.

Thinking, thinking, A-Xing became even more afraid. His hands were shaking, and each stitch became dull.

The master shot his viper-like eyes over, and A-Xing understood the meaning of these eyes, and he became even more afraid; his heart beat violently, and his hands shook violently. While threading the needle, a needle slipped out of his hand and fell to the ground.

As he bent over in panic to pick up the needle, the heavy tree root ruler had already quickly fallen on his head.

At the junction, yellow-green fecal juice dripped onto the cement. The dung trucks were constantly changing, and the fecal juice on the cement gradually increased, eventually converging into many small fecal ponds, the fecal juice flowed horizontally and vertically in the gaps of the cement, expanding its own

range, and finally converging with other yellow fecal ponds, creating a large area of feces.

Commentary

On Poverty 234

— Yin

In this era when the groans of unemployment resonate loudly throughout our distorted and contradictory society, everyone is qualified to talk about "poverty." In my hometown, there are two common sayings: "Better poor than stinky," which is a complaint from the poor, and "Better poor than fierce," which is a sympathetic yet concerned remark from creditors to their debtors.

"Poverty" is indeed the most terrifying thing. In this world where one cannot stand without money, there is truly no room for the poor to survive. Yet, this strange world is filled with the poor, so "poverty" has become a global issue.

In fact, I believe that if a person's small diary has never included a period of "poverty," then their life must be empty and unfulfilling. "Poverty" is not only without shame, but also a stimulating experience. It is like a blazing fire, igniting people's activities and passion for upward mobility. It can compel people to open their eyes wide and see through the ailments of the world, and prompt them to prescribe a "targeted" remedy for this sick world. Furthermore, it can enable people to use their own strength to create many great and astonishing achievements! As for those who steal, rob, or even commit suicide because of "poverty," they are merely shameful displays of individualists without true perspectives or principles, and the most unpromising of the weak.

A Record of Visiting the Eastern Palace 235

— Miaoshen

One day, introduced by Sister Quan, I visited the girls' dormitory of a certain school in this city, the famous Eastern Palace. Afterwards, I found it quite enjoyable. I think many people must sigh in vain, unable to enter due to the strictness of the palace.

Now I will write some of it out for everyone to daydream about.

Upon entering the palace gate, a delicate melody drifted from afar. Listening carefully, it seemed neither like a zither nor a reed pipe. Later, I learned it was a foreign violin. Inside the palace, there were three thousand beauties, each lively and graceful. Some were playing tennis, others were chatting in groups of three or two on the lawn, each with a smiling face, as beautiful and charming as flowers!

Inside the dormitory, all the beds were uniform steel wire beds with tidy bedding, which was quite orderly. However, the fruit peels on the floor were messy, some were chocolate wrappers, and others were melon seed shells, which was not clean at all.

The Collective Phenomenon - Cheng Xiyuan

Almost everyone had some decorations around their bed. Some hung photos of themselves in charming poses; some pasted photos of Chinese and Western movie stars; and some even drew a beautiful schedule and pasted it next to their bed. Everyone's arrangement was unique and quite beautiful.

Under each person's bed, almost everyone had a pair of beautiful, fashionable leather shoes hidden. It is said that these shoes are only worn on Sundays.

Besides books and lecture notes, there were also many movie brochures piled on the desks. Some people even kept these brochures as a collection on their desks.

Female students mostly love to decorate themselves, but I didn't see many cosmetics. According to Sister Quan, because the school authorities forbid it, everyone hid their cosmetics. Each month, the maids take out countless bottles and jars of various cosmetics!

I saw a few people writing very seriously. I said to Sister Quan, "They are very diligent." Sister Quan smiled and said, "They are writing letters. Here, writing letters is more important than reading lecture notes."

It is said that Ms. X is the "queen" of this school. Sister Quan said, "She has extensive social connections and is very capable. Would you like to meet her?" I said, "Okay." After Sister Quan introduced me, I saw that she was indeed beautiful with delicate features. Ms. X was very friendly, and we hit it off immediately. After exchanging names, I asked her:

"You have extensive social connections and are still studying, which shows that you have extraordinary energy. Some people say that just reading books is useless, and one must go into society to personally experience and observe. Is that why you do so well?"

Ms. X smiled slightly and said, "Socializing is certainly indispensable for a person, and society is something no one can live without. However, if socializing becomes too busy, it can also interfere with one's studies, so I am now a bit tired of socializing."

This was truly unexpected. Ms. X, known for her social skills, actually said such a thing.

"I heard that you are the most socially skilled person here, so you must have a very clear understanding of the advantages and disadvantages of socializing. However, in my opinion, the most troublesome and harmful thing during the study period is socializing with the opposite sex!" Ms. X said very frankly, "That's right! I think some men are the most annoying. They are obstacles to our future, the enemies of us women, making us sacrifice! For example, some people say that I am the 'queen' of this school. This is entirely the result of men toying with me, and the reason is that I socialize too much, and they all know me."

"So, you really hate socializing?"

"Yes, I really hate socializing, and I even dislike men somewhat!"

At this point, because it was getting late, Sister Quan called me to go back together. Ms. X even saw us off to the door.

Opening of a Famous Shanghai Socialite's Day 236

— Mengfei

A beautiful woman alone in her fragrant room. Leaning lazily on the cool bed with a charming face. Her eyes are drowsy, still weary. She yawns repeatedly, languidly. Her jade bracelets are crystal clear green. Reflecting the snowy white skin, as white as frost. Her delicate figure is like a fresh flower. Like a peony in the rain, a begonia in spring. She opens her mouth, calling for her maidservant. Wanting to wash and dress with fragrant water. In a flash, a young maid walks in. Pouring water and brewing tea, serving busily. She gets up, washes, and applies rouge and powder. Instantly, the whole room smells fragrant. In the bronze mirror, her beautiful face shines. It shines so brightly that even the slightest flaw disappears. She feels tired after dressing up. Smoking a Baijinlong cigarette, she walks to the window. Next to her, she turns on the electric fan. Instantly, a cool breeze sweeps over her body. She instructs to turn on the radio. Listening quietly to records, full of joy. Some sing Shanghai opera. Some sing comic dialogues. Some sing Peking opera. Some sing Kunqu opera. Nothing but northern and southern tunes. When it sounds good, she smiles slightly. When she hears something funny, she scolds lightly. She rests calmly, feeling at ease. A servant girl brings in bird's nest soup. A bowl of white fungus with added sugar. In the afternoon, she invites her sisters. Playing mahjong in the Central Wind White Board room. When night comes, she feels hot. Riding a motorcycle to enjoy the cool breeze. This is also a natural blessing, surpassing the ordinary.

War and Peace (6) 239

— Linghe

Middle-aged Man A: But you can't say it that way either. In today's world, there is no one who doesn't want money, and besides, if the army doesn't get paid for several months, they still have to eat. How can you expect them not to help themselves?

Old Man: But no matter what, it's wrong to make the common people pay. If they don't get paid, they can ask the officers, why take it out on us?

Middle-aged Man C: That's right. Last year, the army in the county town rioted over pay and killed several officers.

(The sound of a car approaching.)

Middle-aged Man B: Listen! What's that sound?

Old Woman: Oh no! That's not good, the damn planes are coming again.

Old Man: Really? Then we better run!

Middle-aged Man B: No, it's not a plane.

Old Man: Where's the sound coming from? How come I can't hear anything? Ah! Old people are really useless, sometimes they can't even hear thunder.

Middle-aged Man C: (Standing on the pile of wood to the right of the stage) It's a car. Look at the dust. There are two cars, I wonder what they're carrying?

(The sound of the car gets closer and closer, and everyone curiously runs to the left of the stage. Only the Old Man and Middle-aged Man A are still standing in place, looking to the left. Then they hear the sound of the car's horn, and it stops to the left of the stage, but the audience cannot see it. Then there is a clamor of voices. They only hear someone saying:)

Voice: Aren't there two full cars? Who knows how many there are.

Middle-aged Man A: The fighting at the front has been fierce these past few days, almost every day they are transporting wounded soldiers and dead bodies. Old Woman: Heavens! What's going on? Living people sitting on dead bodies, shouting in pain, even if they don't die from the pain, they'll be scared to death.

Move all those who are not dead to this place.

When the wounded soldiers are placed on the ground, they let out agonizing cries. Middle-aged Man C also helps a lightly wounded person up and lets them sit next to the old man. Film Supplement

About the Screenplay of HinPIeWeKes (Part 2) 240

— Bofu

Film Translation Title: "The Way of Independence"

Undoubtedly, in the character of this daughter, the author depicts for us a modern woman with perseverance, brains, and autonomy, breaking the ingrained concepts of sex and the traditional moral ideology. This is exactly the natural development of women as depicted by Ibsen. However, whether a working girl in a remote village in the northern part of England twenty years ago would have such a mindset is indeed questionable. On this point, it must be said that the author, like Ibsen, has an overly romantic color.

However, this play is still worth rereading today, twenty years later. This is not because the author wrote a romantic new woman for us, but because the author's character portrayal depicts a typical capitalist and other characters.

The daughter's struggle is naturally against traditional concepts and ingrained morals, and the person representing this ideology is the father of the young master, a factory owner. He and the daughter's father both started as workers, but after ten years, he has become a millionaire, while the daughter's father is still a worker and has to work in his factory. The contrast between the characters of these two old men is really well depicted. One controls his son with an iron fist, while the other cannot even control his daughter and is even bullied by his wife. The difference in their characters determines their fate in that kind of society. As for the individualistic nature of capitalists, it is even more vividly displayed in the character of this factory owner. He tells his wife that the reason why he works so hard to make money is not because money can buy a wealthy life, but because money is power. So he buys a car for his son, not to show off, but to make people say that his son can afford a car. He also says that his son can spend as much as he wants, but he has to ask him for it. Especially when he finds out about his son's matter, the attitude he takes shows his character even more. Contrasting his character is the future father-in-law of his son. He is also a capitalist, but he is an extreme egoist, the kind of rich and unkind person often seen in Chinese movies. However, the son's father, in addition to wanting to be a rich person, also has ambitions, he also wants to single-handedly support the society they have created. Therefore, he is willing to fight to the death against any moral law that endangers this society. These people are the backbone of the capitalist society. The author was originally from Lancaster, with practical experience, so he was very successful in depicting this kind of person.

Most of the power of this play lies in the dialogue, but the words spoken by the characters are all accented. We already found it difficult when reading the script, and if it were made into a movie, I'm afraid it would be even more difficult to understand. But knowing the origin of this play makes it worth watching. (The End)

Film Review

Review of "Shotgun Pass" 241

— Linghe

Shotgun Pass

It's definitely not an exaggeration to say that Columbia Pictures productions are often disappointing. This is naturally because the producers place too much emphasis on low-level interests. Because of this, they have extracted a lot of money from the masses who have few opportunities to see movies and who have a relatively low level of knowledge. From this point of view, the entrepreneurs of this company may be very proud. But as far as the art of film itself is concerned, no matter from what standpoint, every production should not be made in a crude and shoddy manner. Even when catering to low-level interests, one should try to enrich the content as much as possible, while striving for simplicity in form. On the one hand, it is necessary to make them understand, but on the other hand, it is also necessary to give the audience a good education. Therefore, we cannot equate vulgarity and shallowness with being interesting, nor can we necessarily make them all understandable. Taking this film as an example, the two Shanghainese people sitting behind me were probably very interested in this kind of "one man with a gun" stuff. When they saw Ding Maigai fighting in the village hotel, they only heard one of them say: "This film is nothing!" Later, Ding Maigai found a clump of mud on a rock in the mountains, with traces of belt buckles and bullets on it, and therefore knew that his enemies had ambushed him on this rock, so he took this clump of mud as evidence. But at this point, the two friends behind me couldn't understand, and the one who was speaking kept asking: "Why? Why?" The one answering could only say: "I don't understand either." Therefore, it can be seen that this kind of film still has a lot of gaps for them. As for the content, then this kind of martial arts film will undoubtedly not give them a good impression. The character played by Ding Maigai, for the revenge of his father's death, for the theft of the horses, because he is his own villain, he showed the power of a traitor, punishing the violent and eliminating the evil, and fighting fiercely. That kind of hero from "Seven Swords and Thirteen Knights" is not only laughable, but the chaotic state of no organization and no discipline is giving them a bad lesson. Therefore, I think that if such films continue to be screened "one set after another", many "bloody" "low-level"

friends will definitely run to the mountains to become Robin Hoods who rob the rich and help the poor.

However, then again, when the thing called film is still used as the best production tool by entrepreneurs, it cannot become a tool for educating the masses as we wish. Therefore, it determines that people engaged in culture have an even more important task than criticizing films at the moment.

As for the technical aspects of this film, then I think it's just a lot of horses running back and forth on the screen, and there's nothing to talk about in terms of technique.

Audience Opinions

"Vigor" Short Commentary 242

— Jing Chun

Under this fitting theme, an engaging story unfolds. The protagonist of the play, Li Peilan, viewed through the lens of China's economic structure, is a typical urban housewife. Her family's livelihood depends entirely on her husband's clever financial transactions. From our intuitive observation, it goes without saying that such women are complete idlers; besides readily available enjoyment, they are inherently lazy. This prevalent phenomenon of women's decline is a serious problem for Chinese women. However, we should not be pessimistic about the future of women because of this. In recent years, haven't social scientists been giving enthusiastic guidance? But theory is theory; without concrete and vivid stimulation, the women's movement remains in a state of slow progress.

Now, we urgently need various cultural sectors to provide opportunities for discussing this issue. After watching "Vigor," I feel that it has provided a clear and insightful answer to this bleak problem of women. It picks out a typical female figure, "Li Peilan," from among the thousands of women groping in the dark; this woman is not a superhuman but a character who seizes opportunities for self-realization.

We see in her the determination to escape perilous circumstances and an unwavering will. With hardship, she uses her delicate hands to accomplish great things, founding a sewing factory with the aim of providing relief to unemployed women, not to exploit the sweat and blood of workers, but to realize their "self-sufficiency."

Seen in this way, we can say that Li Peilan is a new woman with social consciousness.

Of course, this performance of "Vigor" will provide a great impetus for the Chinese women's movement. (Chapter missing)

My Thoughts After Watching "Vigor" 243

— Lin Xiumei

Shao Zuiweng's past directorial works, apart from "Yunlan Girl," have rarely been surprisingly contributory. Now, after watching "Vigor," I feel that Shao Zuiweng has progressed compared to before.

"Vigor"'s directing technique has gained new achievements, and the use of contrast is also very clever. The advertisement says it is Shao Zuiweng's masterpiece of changing his style. Although the words "masterpiece" may be an exaggeration, the "change of style" is real.

Just from the title "Vigor," we can see how full of vitality it is. The development of the story, from beginning to end, tells a group of women how to be independent, how to strive, and not to rely on men, not to be playthings of men, but to work hard and diligently, and there will be hope of success in the future. Li Peilan is an example. At the same time, it also has a profound depiction of the darkness of modern society and the snobbery of human relationships.

But the film also has many shortcomings, such as Li Peilan hitting a gangster with an ashtray, and the gangster falling to the ground in response and lying motionless. In reason, this would not happen. After Wu Daqing went bankrupt, when he went to find Li Peilan, the slogans posted on the road seemed to be aimed specifically at Wu, and there were no other pedestrians on the road except Wu, which is also not very reasonable. Also, Wu Daqing's living room seems too grand and magnificent, because Daqing is just a small bourgeois, and he would not live in such a large building.

The sound and cinematography is average. The light is a bit too soft in some places, but it is not a major flaw. This film and Lianhua's "The Light of Motherhood" are both successful works of domestic films. (Chapter missing)

After Watching "Vigor" 244

— Yu Jian

(Above omitted) The compilation of the story, it cannot be denied, has found a fresh theme. However, I always feel that there are still many places that are not enough. I think perhaps the screenwriter deliberately did it this way, because if it wasn't written this way, it wouldn't have gotten such a good ending. The screenwriter is probably aware of the other insufficiencies, but due to various restrictions, he had no choice but to say, "Let it be."

The sound is very clear, which adds a lot to the film. However, there seem to be a few too many songs.

I don't know if it was due to the limitations of the story or something else, but I feel that the performances of each actor were just average, although I didn't feel that anyone acted "too badly." In this film, Chen Yumei can be considered hardworking, but I don't think she was particularly brilliant.

The scenery is well-matched. The cinematography is not bad, and there are a few clever shots that are really admirable.

One thing is that some places feel incoherent. Of course, intricate interlacing is indispensable. But reaching a point of incoherence is not a good phenomenon. Although this film did not leave a deep impression on me, it already has a good tendency, which I cannot deny. This point made me feel quite happy when I lay in bed. (Chapter missing)

Commentary on "Vigor" 245

— Dai Dai

The results of "Vigor" seem to have improved compared to Tianyi's previous productions, and the sound is also quite clear. A special commentary is as follows:

The protagonist, Chen Yumei, plays Li Peilan, a woman struggling in an adverse environment. At first, her performance of being oppressed, and hearing her husband Wu Daqing's sleep talking, "frowning and pondering," and "suspicions arising" are very appropriate to her role. Later, the plot turns tense when she is indignant at her unvirtuous husband and takes her son back to her mother's home. From this scene onwards, Chen Yumei's performance method also takes a sharp turn, becoming extremely resolute and brave. From beginning to end, it is wonderful and powerful. Overall, Chen Yumei's performance in "Vigor" is the most successful.

In terms of supporting roles, Yuan Meiyun's performance as Li Peilan's sister is very good, but unfortunately, there are very few performance opportunities. But she also sang two songs, "A Butterfly and a Bee" and "Little Baby," which were still graceful and pleasant to listen to. Zhang Zhenduo's Wu Daqing, in the first half, performs the absurd behavior of a general small bourgeois. Some of his actions seem too frivolous. In the second half, his performance of the frustration and suffering after "bankruptcy" and the diligence and sincerity after being taken in by Li Peilan is better. Lu Xia plays Wu Daqing's mistress, Lao San, and her performance is quite hardworking, but it is a bit too much. Others, such as Wang Huijuan, Ye Qiuxin, Ma Dongwu, Zhu Tianhong, etc., all play their roles in this film competently. Generally speaking, there are no major flaws. The director has small cleverness, and the contrast is excellent. The cinematography is average.

Movie Novel The Morning Glory (13) 246

— Ma Teng

She said to Xue Lidan, "Please rest assured. I will definitely do my best to satisfy you." She then asked Xue in a very soft voice why he was so good to her. Xue Lidan said that one day he would tell her, but now was not the time for her to understand. Their eyes met, and they were silently speechless. I smiled slightly. Xue Lidan looked at her with deep affection, then bowed and withdrew.

The play opened, and I, Lu Lanse, took to the stage to perform. Xue Lidan stood backstage, clutching a handful of sweat, afraid to breathe as he watched. Tears filled his eyes, and he didn't know what the taste in his throat was. It wasn't until the curtain fell that applause like thunder filled the theater. The curtain rose again, and I bowed to receive the respect of the entire audience. This happened several times until the applause gradually subsided. Then he squeezed to the back, where it was already full of people congratulating and admiring her. He finally approached her, took her hand, and stared at her without saying a word. Then he lowered his head and kissed her forehead, saying, "I!" I asked with shame, "Do you really like me?" Xue Lidan said, "Your performance was too superb." I asked him what Yishidun thought. Xue Lidan told her that Yishidun was so happy because her performance was unexpected that he was going crazy. He would come to negotiate the contract in a moment. The drama critic Lawrence also came to congratulate her. He said that he had already telegraphed his newspaper, preparing many good adjectives to use. Lawrence left, and I and Xue Lidan were overjoyed, because Lawrence was a famous sharp tongue on Broadway, and he usually didn't say good things about people. Then Yishidun came. He took her hand and said, "My dear, I really have no words to say. You are a miracle. I've been in the theater for so many years, this is my happiest night." After Yishidun finished speaking, he blamed himself, saying that he had never given her a chance before. He was so sorry for her that he was ashamed. I comforted him instead, telling him not to talk about the past. Yishidun gradually felt more at ease. He told her that from now on, she would be under the protection of his career. He added, "This is all business." I followed him and said, "It's all business," feeling very sad in my heart. Would the old wounds in my heart never heal? The door rang again, and Haijiesi stuck his head in and asked, "May I come in?" I couldn't say anything at the time and just nodded to him. Haijiesi came in, and I said to the three of them, "You three are the benefactors who made me famous, and I will repay you in the future so that you will not be disappointed in me." Haijiesi looked at her deeply, then said very sincerely, "You should say that a little slower." Then he explained a reason. (To be continued)

Home
